<p><i><b>Recovery</b></i> is the seventh <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album" class="mw-redirect">studio album</a> by American rapper <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>. It was released on June 18, 2010, by <a href="/wiki/Shady_Records" title="Shady Records">Shady Records</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a> as the follow-up to Eminem's <i><a href="/wiki/Relapse_(Eminem_album)" title="Relapse (Eminem album)">Relapse</a></i> (2009). Originally planned to be released as <i>Relapse 2</i>, the album was renamed to <i>Recovery</i> when Eminem found the music of the new album different from its predecessor.</p>
<p>Production of the album took place during 2009 to 2010 at several recording studios and was handled by various record producers, including <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Just_Blaze" title="Just Blaze">Just Blaze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boi-1da" title="Boi-1da">Boi-1da</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jonsin" title="Jim Jonsin">Jim Jonsin</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khalil" title="DJ Khalil">DJ Khalil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kon_Artis" title="Kon Artis" class="mw-redirect">Mr. Porter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>. Eminem also collaborated with artists such as <a href="/wiki/Pink_(singer)" title="Pink (singer)">Pink</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> for the album. <i>Recovery</i> featured more introspective and emotional content than its predecessor and the theme of the album revolved around his positive changes, anxiety, and emotional drives. For the promotion of the album, he featured in TV shows and performed the album's songs live on televised shows, at awards ceremonies, musical events and also headed <a href="/wiki/The_Recovery_Tour" title="The Recovery Tour">The Recovery Tour</a>.</p>
<p>The album received generally positive reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>, who complimented Eminem's rapping and performance on the album, although some criticized its inconsistency and production. <i>Recovery</i> debuted at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, selling 741,000 copies in its first week and stayed at number one for seven non-consecutive weeks. It also peaked inside the top ten of several other countries and was the best-selling album of 2010 worldwide. By October 2011, the album had sold approximately 10 million copies worldwide. <i>Recovery</i> has earned Eminem <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards" class="mw-redirect">American Music Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" title="Billboard Music Awards" class="mw-redirect"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Music_Awards" title="Detroit Music Awards">Detroit Music Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards" class="mw-redirect">Grammy Awards</a>, while it was nominated at <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juno_Awards" title="Juno Awards" class="mw-redirect">Juno Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards_Japan" title="MTV Video Music Awards Japan">MTV Video Music Awards Japan</a>.</p>
<p>The lead single "<a href="/wiki/Not_Afraid" title="Not Afraid">Not Afraid</a>", released on April 29, 2010, sold 380,000 digital downloads in its first week debuting at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and earned Eminem a Grammy for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance">Best Rap Solo Performance</a>. "<a href="/wiki/Love_The_Way_You_Lie" title="Love The Way You Lie" class="mw-redirect">Love The Way You Lie</a>" featuring Rihanna reached the top spot in over 20 countries and stayed at number one on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for seven consecutive weeks. With sales of over 6 million in the United States and 10.25 million worldwide, it is Eminem's best selling single to date. He collaborated with Lil Wayne for "<a href="/wiki/No_Love" title="No Love">No Love</a>". "<a href="/wiki/Space_Bound" title="Space Bound">Space Bound</a>" was released as the fourth and the final single. Four other unreleased songs from the album also charted on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_production">Background and production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recovery_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background and production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg/200px-Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg" width="200" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg/300px-Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg/400px-Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg 2x" data-file-width="454" data-file-height="520" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eminem_at_DJ_hero_party_with_d12.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Eminem first planned the release of <i>Relapse 2</i> as a sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Relapse_(Eminem_album)" title="Relapse (Eminem album)">Relapse</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In a press release, Eminem explained that he and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> had recorded a considerable amount of music while recording <i><a href="/wiki/Relapse_(Eminem_album)" title="Relapse (Eminem album)">Relapse</a></i> (2009), thus, "putting out <i>Relapse 2</i> will let everyone get all of the best stuff."<sup id="cite_ref-MTVMay19_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVMay19-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Angela Yee's <a href="/wiki/Shade_45" title="Shade 45">Shade 45</a> interview with Eminem on April 23, 2009, <i>Relapse 2</i> was to be a continuation of <i>Relapse</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> During the interview Eminem also confirmed "It's extremely close to being finished, it just depends on how many songs I want to put on it."<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> He called into Shade 45 and said he was in the studio finishing up the album.<sup id="cite_ref-Voodoo_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voodoo-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Recording sessions for the album took place during 2009 to 2010 at several recording studios, including Allure Sound in <a href="/wiki/Oak_Park,_Michigan" title="Oak Park, Michigan">Oak Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, 54 Sound and Effigy Studios in <a href="/wiki/Ferndale,_Michigan" title="Ferndale, Michigan">Ferndale</a>, Michigan, <a href="/wiki/Black_Chiney" title="Black Chiney">Black Chiney</a> Studios in <a href="/wiki/Lauderdale_Lakes,_Florida" title="Lauderdale Lakes, Florida">Lauderdale Lakes</a>, Florida, Boi-1da Studio in <a href="/wiki/Ajax,_Ontario" title="Ajax, Ontario">Ajax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Canada, Playhouse in <a href="/wiki/Parkland,_Florida" title="Parkland, Florida">Parkland</a>, Florida, Avex Honolulu Studio in <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a>, Hawaii, Encore Studios in <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank</a>, California, Sun Studios in <a href="/wiki/Temple_Bar,_Dublin" title="Temple Bar, Dublin">Temple Bar</a>, Dublin, and Shake 'Em Down Studios in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-liner_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liner-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>When premiering his debut single, "<a href="/wiki/Not_Afraid" title="Not Afraid">Not Afraid</a>", Eminem also let listeners know that "there were not any skits on the album" (so the album would contain more songs than his previous studio albums).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> He described a song titled "Insult to Injury", in which Eminem performs in his normal voice, as a sequel to "Underground," the final track from the previous album, <i>Relapse</i>. A song on the album "Hit Me With Your Best Shot" featured his rap group <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bizarre_(rapper)" title="Bizarre (rapper)">Bizarre</a> of D12 said the new song shows the group's strength despite the death of founder <a href="/wiki/Proof_(rapper)" title="Proof (rapper)">Proof</a> by stating: "We're still family, but everybody's got their own situations going on," he added. "No matter what y'all do, you can't hold D12 down. We've been through a lot of shit, but we're still gonna come back and recover."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Alchemist:_High_and_Mighty_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Alchemist:_High_and_Mighty-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As for guests on the album, Eminem had said back while the album was still titled <i>Relapse 2</i>, he worked with both Dr. Dre and <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> on the album. <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royce_da_5%279%22" title="Royce da 5'9&quot;">Royce da 5'9"</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cashis" title="Cashis">Cashis</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> had been speculated as possible features on the album. However, none of these artists are actually featured; <i>Recovery</i> only featured guest appearances by rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> and solo singers Kobe, <a href="/wiki/Pink_(singer)" title="Pink (singer)">Pink</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-liner_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liner-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> He decided to include Pink on "Won't Back Down" after recording his parts first because he "felt like she would smash this record".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> On the bonus track "Session One", Eminem features supergroup <a href="/wiki/Slaughterhouse_(group)" title="Slaughterhouse (group)">Slaughterhouse</a>, signed with Shady Records.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/DJ_Whoo_Kid" title="DJ Whoo Kid">DJ Whoo Kid</a> heard some songs from the album and stated that "<a href="/wiki/The_Warning_(Eminem_song)" title="The Warning (Eminem song)">The Warning</a>" is a diss record to <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, and was not as intense as the entire album would be, saying the album is 'maniacal'.<sup id="cite_ref-DJ_Woo_Kid_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DJ_Woo_Kid-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem appeared on <a href="/wiki/Shade_45" title="Shade 45">Shade 45</a> with <a href="/wiki/DJ_Whoo_Kid" title="DJ Whoo Kid">DJ Whoo Kid</a> where he stated that a track with 50 Cent, in which the two rap together on verses, existed.<sup id="cite_ref-shade45_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shade45-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> He also confirmed both <a href="/wiki/Just_Blaze" title="Just Blaze">Just Blaze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denaun_Porter" title="Denaun Porter" class="mw-redirect">Mr. Porter</a> as producers of the album.<sup id="cite_ref-shade45_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shade45-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2009, Eminem said that he expected the release of his new album during the fourth quarter of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Voodoo_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voodoo-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> It was slated to be the second Eminem album released in 2009, after <i>Relapse</i>, but was pushed back to 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-refill_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-refill-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2009, he stated that he would re-release <i>Relapse</i>, with extra songs, to hold fans over for the release of <i>Relapse 2</i> in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-refill_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-refill-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> and was voted as the most anticipated album of fall 2009 by <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <i>Billboard</i>, he said that he would listen to his previous releases like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marshall_Mathers_LP" title="The Marshall Mathers LP">The Marshall Mathers LP</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Eminem_Show" title="The Eminem Show">The Eminem Show</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Encore_(Eminem_song)" title="Encore (Eminem song)">Encore</a></i>, and would "ask [himself], 'Why don't my music feel like this anymore?'" He later recorded material that could constitute three or four studio albums and stated that; "I must have gone through 200–300 beats, for the album and chose 100 of them and recorded it."<sup id="cite_ref-Old_albums_helped_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Old_albums_helped-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes_and_composition">Themes and composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recovery_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Themes and composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa; background-color:#f9f9f9;">

<td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em;"><span style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>

<p>The album was dedicated "To anyone who's in a dark place tryin' to get out. Keep your head up... It does get better!"  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>]<sup id="cite_ref-CD_Booklet_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CD_Booklet-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem, in an interview with <i>Billboard</i>, described that he was in "full-blown addiction" at the time of recording <i>Encore</i>, while he felt happy and "first got sober" during recording <i>Relapse</i> as he was no more an addict. However, he felt that while recording <i>Relapse</i>, he was not "paying attention to what the average listener might like or not like." <a href="/wiki/Just_Blaze" title="Just Blaze">Just Blaze</a>, the first producer of the album stated that, "[Eminem] already knew what sort of mistakes he has made with the previous album and where he wanted to go from there." Thus, <i>Recovery</i> was more "emotionally driven" than <i>Relapse</i>, which was, as he explains, "[just] rap records".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's artwork featured two covers: One with Eminem walking down a country road and another with him sitting in a transparent living room in the middle of <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Center" title="Renaissance Center">Renaissance Center</a> in the background. The album's liner featured pictures of Eminem such as a picture of him <a href="/wiki/Prayer" title="Prayer">praying</a> and him posing without a shirt on.<sup id="cite_ref-CD_Booklet_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CD_Booklet-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album opens with "Cold Wind Blows" in which Eminem sings regarding his "doomed love for his ex-wife" and on "settling scores with rival celebs".<sup id="cite_ref-Rosen_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In "Talkin’ 2 Myself", he states the harm caused to his image with lyrics such as: "Encore’ I was on drugs, ‘Relapse’ I was flushing them out."<sup id="cite_ref-Caramanica_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caramanica-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> "On Fire" shows "a murder-and-dismemberment fantasy" with gruesome rhymes<sup id="cite_ref-Rosen_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Won%27t_Back_Down_(Eminem_song)" title="Won't Back Down (Eminem song)">Won't Back Down</a>" which featured Pink was a <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> song.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> "W.T.P." ("White-Trash Party") sees his singing to go back to his early records with lighter and simple rhythmic frame,<sup id="cite_ref-Caramanica_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caramanica-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> while "Going Through Changes", using <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>'s "Changes", depicts Eminem's sorrow and shows himself being trapped due to fame.<sup id="cite_ref-Kot_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kot-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> "Not Afraid" which is a mid-tempo song, focuses on a positive change from Eminem's past experiences, including an end to drug abuse, feuds and violence.<sup id="cite_ref-eh_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eh-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Idolator commented that the song was based on the "dark days Eminem has lived through", and "he seems to be at peace with himself now."<sup id="cite_ref-ins_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ins-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> A writer for <a href="/wiki/MuchMusic" title="MuchMusic">MuchMusic</a> website noted that Eminem chose to use his Marshall Mathers ego for the song, rather than Slim Shady.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/No_Love" title="No Love">No Love</a>" features Lil Wayne as a <a href="/wiki/Hype_man" title="Hype man">hype man</a> which is followed by Eminem's verses which according to Sam Wolfson of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> are "the best verses of his career."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The meaning of "<a href="/wiki/Space_Bound" title="Space Bound">Space Bound</a>" is not obvious or completely clear and according to <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Grey" title="Sasha Grey">Sasha Grey</a> who is featured in its video, the meaning can be interpreted "in many ways".<sup id="cite_ref-The_Source_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Source-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Jim Jonsin of MTV spoke about Eminem's two egos seen in the video and compared it to <a href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette" title="Alanis Morissette">Alanis Morissette</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ironic_(song)#Music_video" title="Ironic (song)">"Ironic" video</a> while Grey believed that the alternate Eminem who appears in the car is his subconscious.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Source_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Source-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jim_MTV_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jim_MTV-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> "Cinderella Man" with a "festive beat" had "the template of every album since <i>Encore</i> (2004)", with many minor keys and traces of <a href="/wiki/Grunge_rock" title="Grunge rock" class="mw-redirect">post-grunge rock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rosen_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> "25 to Life" shows his discomfiture and depicts that the "selfish bitch" pulling him back "these days is rap itself."<sup id="cite_ref-O.27Neal_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Neal-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the lyrics being tighter throughout the album, "So Bad" and "Almost Famous" views his other side of Slim Shady; his alter ego.<sup id="cite_ref-Caramanica_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caramanica-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The hip-hop ballad "<a href="/wiki/Love_The_Way_You_Lie" title="Love The Way You Lie" class="mw-redirect">Love The Way You Lie</a>" describes a couple's refusal to separate despite having an abusive relationship. Rihanna sings the chorus again, backed by an <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">electric guitar</a> and a piano,<sup id="cite_ref-sosii_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sosii-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> while acoustic guitar, violin and pounding drums accompany Eminem's verses.<sup id="cite_ref-sosii_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sosii-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The singing of Rihanna despite of being without <a href="/wiki/Vibrato" title="Vibrato">vibrato</a>, her voice "shows grief and regret".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Towards the end he claims his influence, by "fevered rhymes" on "You’re Never Over".<sup id="cite_ref-Kot_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kot-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recovery_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large screen with the silhouette of a man, seated with two pistols, is in the center. Surrounding it are screens showing Eminem, who is to the right of Rihanna. The latter is holding a microphone and has short red hair." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg/290px-Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg" width="290" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg/435px-Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg/580px-Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="703" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eminem_and_Rihanna_in_Love_the_Way_You_Lie2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Eminem and <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> performing "Love the Way You Lie" at <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2010" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2010">E3 2010</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Recovery</i> was confirmed during a press release by Eminem's label on March 5, 2010, and was originally titled <i>Relapse 2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTVMay19_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVMay19-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-recovery_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recovery-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> On April 13, 2010, Eminem <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeted</a> "There is no <i>Relapse 2</i>" to his followers. It was followed by him tweeting "Recovery" with a link to his website. Eminem said "I had originally planned for <i>Relapse 2</i> to come out last year. But as I kept recording and working with new producers, the idea of a sequel to <i>Relapse</i> started to make less and less sense to me, and I wanted to make a completely new album. The music on <i>Recovery</i> came out very different from <i>Relapse</i>, and I think it deserves its own title."<sup id="cite_ref-recovery_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recovery-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> He later released a <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyle</a> titled "Despicable" over "<a href="/wiki/Over_(Drake_song)" title="Over (Drake song)">Over</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)" class="mw-redirect">Drake</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Beamer,_Benz,_or_Bentley" title="Beamer, Benz, or Bentley">Beamer, Benz, or Bentley</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Juelz_Santana" title="Juelz Santana">Juelz Santana</a> as promo for the first single, "<a href="/wiki/Not_Afraid" title="Not Afraid">Not Afraid</a>", which debuted on <a href="/wiki/Shade_45" title="Shade 45">Shade 45</a> on April 29.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-radiorelease_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radiorelease-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Eventually, <i>Recovery</i> was released on June 18 in the Europe and on June 21 in the United States and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Eminem has done multiple interviews such as with <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull" title="Red Bull">Red Bull</a> in promotion of the album. A commercial for <i>Recovery</i> premiered during Game 6 of the <a href="/wiki/2010_NBA_Finals" title="2010 NBA Finals">2010 NBA Finals</a>. It featured <a href="/wiki/Vince_Offer" title="Vince Offer">Vince Offer</a> from the Slap Chop commercials in a parody of his commercials.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> A <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty:_Black_Ops" title="Call of Duty: Black Ops">Call of Duty: Black Ops</a></i> ad with "Won't Back Down" was released; the song also appeared in the game as an <a href="/wiki/Easter_egg" title="Easter egg">easter egg</a>. On June 15, Eminem appeared among other artists including <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a> for <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>'s press conference during the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2010" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2010">Electronic Entertainment Expo 2010</a> with Rihanna where the duo performed "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie" title="Love the Way You Lie">Love the Way You Lie</a>". In addition, Eminem performed "<a href="/wiki/Lose_Yourself" title="Lose Yourself">Lose Yourself</a>", "Not Afraid", and premiered "Won't Back Down" for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-Eminem.2C_Rihanna.2C_Usher_kick_off_Activision.E2.80.99s_E3_event_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eminem.2C_Rihanna.2C_Usher_kick_off_Activision.E2.80.99s_E3_event-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Eminem featured on <a href="/wiki/E!" title="E!">E!</a> during their Daily 10 show in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Sparks" title="Clinton Sparks">Clinton Sparks</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and also appeared in a skit on <a href="/wiki/The_Soup" title="The Soup">The Soup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> He performed songs from the album as well as his previous songs at various events such as the 2010 <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2010 MTV Video Music Awards">2010 MTV Video Music Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-VMA_2010_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VMA_2010-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2010" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2010">Electronic Entertainment Expo 2010</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MTVE3_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTVE3-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bonnaroo_Music_Festival" title="Bonnaroo Music Festival">Bonnaroo Music Festival</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Bonnaroo_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonnaroo-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bil_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bil-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/T_in_the_Park" title="T in the Park">T in the Park</a><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Group" title="Virgin Group">Virgin Group</a>'s <a href="/wiki/V_Festival" title="V Festival">V Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-v2011_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-v2011-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> He also headed <a href="/wiki/The_Recovery_Tour" title="The Recovery Tour">The Recovery Tour</a>; a series of European, American and Australian concerts in support of the album and its predecessor <i><a href="/wiki/Relapse_(Eminem_album)" title="Relapse (Eminem album)">Relapse</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recovery_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first single, "<a href="/wiki/Not_Afraid" title="Not Afraid">Not Afraid</a>" was released on Shade 45 and has received free streaming on Eminem's website since then.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The song sold 380,000 digital downloads in its first week, and became the sixteenth song in the history of the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> to debut at number one;<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> it is only the second hip hop single to debut at number one following "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_Missing_You" title="I'll Be Missing You">I'll Be Missing You</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Puff Daddy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faith_Evans" title="Faith Evans">Faith Evans</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/112_(band)" title="112 (band)" class="mw-redirect">112</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> It has sold more than 5 million copies in US.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The official music video of "Not Afraid" which was directed by <a href="/wiki/Rich_Lee" title="Rich Lee">Rich Lee</a>, premiered on June 5, 2010 on <a href="/wiki/Vevo" title="Vevo">Vevo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video, shot in <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a>, New Jersey, won the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Male_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Male Video">MTV Video Music Award for Best Male Video</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2010 MTV Video Music Awards">2010 MTV Video Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The song also won the award of the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance">Best Rap Solo Performance</a> at the 53rd Grammy Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> praised Eminem's commitment on his new music and lyrical ability noting "Over a dark, operatic beat, Eminem delivers rhymes that are typically acrobatic – and typically heavy-handed. But the anger has a gathering quality."<sup id="cite_ref-Dolan_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dolan-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The second single was released on August 9, 2010 titled "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie" title="Love the Way You Lie">Love the Way You Lie</a>", which featured <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The song debuted at number two on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and later peaked number one. The song gave <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> his fourth US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 number one and Rihanna her seventh. It also claimed the top spot on over 20 other charts worldwide. "Love the Way You Lie" went on to be number one on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for seven consecutive weeks and is certified Diamond by <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a> and has sold more than 6 million in US.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The song became Eminem's best-selling single of all time, selling 9.3 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kahn" title="Joseph Kahn">Joseph Kahn</a> directed the music video which premiered on August 5, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-mtv_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The video starred <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Monaghan" title="Dominic Monaghan">Dominic Monaghan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megan_Fox" title="Megan Fox">Megan Fox</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Love-hate_relationship" title="Love-hate relationship" class="mw-redirect">love-hate relationship</a>. Michael Menachem from <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> commented that "Rihanna's chorus is exquisitely melodic and surprisingly hopeful, complementing the turmoil of Em's dark, introspective rant."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was performed at the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2010 MTV Video Music Awards">2010 MTV Video Music Awards</a> and was voted the best performer of the ceremony in an MTV poll, earning 34 percent of votes.<sup id="cite_ref-VMA_2010_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VMA_2010-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/No_Love" title="No Love">No Love</a>", which features American rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, was the third single released on October 5, 2010. "No Love" featured sample of "<a href="/wiki/What_Is_Love_(Haddaway_song)" title="What Is Love (Haddaway song)">What Is Love</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Haddaway" title="Haddaway">Haddaway</a>, which was done by producer <a href="/wiki/Just_Blaze" title="Just Blaze">Just Blaze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The song peaked number 23 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and stayed on the charts for 20 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-sc_Billboardhot100_Eminem_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sc_Billboardhot100_Eminem-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Robinson_(director)" title="Chris Robinson (director)">Chris Robinson</a>, premiered on September 30 via Vevo and various <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> networks.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The video was about a young school boy who was bullied but had the urge to stand up after being motivated by listening to songs by Eminem and Lil Wayne. They performed "No Love" on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> on December 18, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Space_Bound" title="Space Bound">Space Bound</a>" was released as the fourth and final single from the album on March 18, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> English songwriter <a href="/wiki/Steve_McEwan" title="Steve McEwan">Steve McEwan</a> provided additional vocals in the <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">chorus</a> of the song.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The single did not enter US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, however was certified Gold in United States on February 9, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video for "Space Bound" was shot in February 2011 by Joseph Kahn.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The uncensored music video was released on June 24, 2011 at 5 PM EST on <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes</a> only and the official video then premiered on <a href="/wiki/Vevo" title="Vevo">Vevo</a> on June 27 at 3 AM EST.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The plot stars actress <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Grey" title="Sasha Grey">Sasha Grey</a> and Eminem in a relationship which ends violently; the video caused controversy for a bloody scene in which Eminem shoots himself.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The video was slammed by British <a href="/wiki/Nonviolence" title="Nonviolence">anti-violence</a> campaigners.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Anti-violence group, Mothers Against Violence, told the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i>, "It's all about the money with these videos. Eminem isn't thinking about the families affected."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video was then analyzed by Sasha Grey and the song's producer, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jonsin" title="Jim Jonsin">Jim Jonsin</a> who both agreed that the video had no certain message, but could be interpreted "in many ways".<sup id="cite_ref-The_Source_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Source-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jim_MTV_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jim_MTV-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Songs "25 to Life", "<a href="/wiki/Won%27t_Back_Down_(Eminem_song)" title="Won't Back Down (Eminem song)">Won't Back Down</a>", "Talkin' 2 Myself", and "Cold Wind Blows" also debuted on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 without release as singles.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chart_history_Hot_100_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chart_history_Hot_100-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> "Cinderella Man" was certified Gold in the United States on February 17, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recovery_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="4/5 stars"><img alt="4/5 stars" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" <td scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="1.5/5 stars"><img alt="1.5/5 stars" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" width="11" height="11" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" width="11" height="11" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110" /></span><sup id="cite_ref-Richards_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richards-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></td>

<tr>
<td scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle">7/10<sup id="cite_ref-Ingrim_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ingrim-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Recovery</i> received generally positive reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream critics, the album received an <a href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean" class="mw-redirect">average</a> score of 63, based on 28 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic" class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a>'s David Jeffries praised Eminem's performance as potent and energetic, and said that the album "may be flawed ... but he hasn't sounded this unfiltered and proud since <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marshall_Mathers_LP" title="The Marshall Mathers LP">The Marshall Mathers LP</a></i>".<sup id="cite_ref-Jeffries_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeffries-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Neil McCormick of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> commended him for addressing more mature, introspective subject matter and successfully "framing his misogyny, homophobia and all-round bigotry with an undeniable sense of empathy and humanity."<sup id="cite_ref-McCormick_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCormick-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jody_Rosen" title="Jody Rosen">Jody Rosen</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, called it Eminem's "most casual-sounding album in years" and said that he "sounds content to be rap's wittiest head case."<sup id="cite_ref-Rosen_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Sam Wolfson of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> called him "self aware, technically advanced, intelligent, able to go at speeds other than full throttle".<sup id="cite_ref-Wolfson_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfson-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Sean O'Neal of <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> felt that his lively raps make up for the "endless atonement metaphors" that occasionally weigh down the album.<sup id="cite_ref-O.27Neal_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Neal-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kitty_Empire" title="Kitty Empire">Kitty Empire</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>, said that it is "better than average" as a "latterday Eminem album" that shows, "in bursts, Eminem's health is very nearly rude."<sup id="cite_ref-Empire_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Empire-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MSN_Music" title="MSN Music">MSN Music</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> said that, although the cleverness "varies" and the themes "rarely" upheld by his "long-recessive sense of play", the album is a comeback "for Eminem, not Slim Shady—and for Marshall at his most martial. His most confessional as well".<sup id="cite_ref-Christgau_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christgau-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a mixed review, Jon Caramanica of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> regarded Eminem as "frustratingly limited in his topical range" and called <i>Recovery</i> "the most insular of all his releases".<sup id="cite_ref-Caramanica_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caramanica-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> commented that "there's nothing here quite as witty or engaging as" on his previous work.<sup id="cite_ref-Gill_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gill-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a>'s Jayson Greene perceived a lack of lyrical depth and wrote "for the first time in his career, he actually sounds <i>clumsy</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-Greene_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greene-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kot" title="Greg Kot">Greg Kot</a> said that it lacks <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hooks</a> and fun: "The subversive humor is long gone, and his cultural references ... remain dated".<sup id="cite_ref-Kot_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kot-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>'s M.T. Richards also found Eminem's pop culture references "inane" and called the album's material "unsurprisingly hollow" with punchlines that "rarely resonate".<sup id="cite_ref-Richards_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richards-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writer Jeff Weiss found his rhyme schemes "dazzling" and wordplay "clever", but panned its production as "monochromatic and monotonous".<sup id="cite_ref-Weiss_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weiss-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Paul MacInnes said that the music lacks consistency because of a "piecemeal approach to production" and "fashionable soft-rock samples".<sup id="cite_ref-MacInnes_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacInnes-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recovery_(Eminem_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The album debuted at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, with first-week sales of 741,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> It became Eminem's sixth album to debut at number one in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> In its second week of release it remained at number-one and sold 313,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> It also entered at number one on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Billboard</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums" class="mw-redirect">R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> and <a href="/wiki/Top_Rap_Albums" title="Top Rap Albums" class="mw-redirect">Rap Albums</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-R.26B_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R.26B-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rap_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rap-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> In its ninth week of release the album remained at number one for its seventh non-consecutive week and sold 116,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-Baller_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baller-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> By March 2011, the album was number one on the all-time list of albums with the most digital sales, with over 922,000 copies digitally sold at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> As of July 2011, the album broke the digital record and became the first album to sell one million digital copies.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> It held the record for most digital albums sold, but was later outsold by <a href="/wiki/Adele_(singer)" title="Adele (singer)" class="mw-redirect">Adele</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/21_(Adele_album)" title="21 (Adele album)">21</a></i> album.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 18, 2011, the album was certified triple platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> in shipments and sales.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> As of November 13, 2013, the album has sold 4,513,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Since its United States release, the album spent a total of 27 weeks in the top 10 of the Billboard 200, which is more than any other hip-hop album since 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> It spent seven weeks at number one in both the US &amp; UK amongst other nations.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, selling 140,000 copies in its first week in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In Canada, the album sold 85,000 copies in its first week and debuted at number one on <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canada's Albums Chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The album spent six consecutive weeks at number one,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> and retook the top spot after one week at number two.<sup id="cite_ref-Eminem_Canada_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eminem_Canada-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> As of August 18, 2010, the album has sold 277,000 copies in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Eminem_Canada_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eminem_Canada-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In Japan, <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> recorded a debut of number six with 20,678 units sold.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> It also went gold in its first week in New Zealand and Australia, debuting at number one in both countries.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ARIA24_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA24-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The album has since sold over 210,000 copies in Australia, certifying it triple platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-ARIA_Top_50_Albums_Chart_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_Top_50_Albums_Chart-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of its release year, <i>Recovery</i> had sold over 5.7 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> It was one of the best-selling album of 2010 in the United States with 3.4 million copies, and it had sold 2.3 million copies in other territories for a total of 5.7 million copies worldwide by December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a>, it was also the best-selling album of 2010 worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was the best-selling album in Canada in 2010 selling 435,000 copies; more than double the album in second place.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Recovery</i> was the third best-selling album of 2010 in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Since its release in 2010, the album has sold 4.5 million copies in the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> and over 10 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<dt>Sample credits</dt>
</dl>
<p>Information taken from <i>Recovery</i> liner notes:<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"Cold Wind Blows" contains elements from "Patriotic Song" performed by Gringo</li>
<li>"On Fire" contains a sample of "Peace and Love" as performed by <a href="/wiki/Mandrill_(band)" title="Mandrill (band)">Mandrill</a></li>
<li>"Going Through Changes" contains a sample of "<a href="/wiki/Changes_(Black_Sabbath_song)" title="Changes (Black Sabbath song)">Changes</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a></li>
<li>"No Love" features a sample of "<a href="/wiki/What_Is_Love_(Haddaway_song)" title="What Is Love (Haddaway song)">What Is Love</a>" performed by <a href="/wiki/Haddaway" title="Haddaway">Haddaway</a></li>
<li>"Space Bound" features an interpolation of "<a href="/wiki/Drive_(R.E.M._song)" title="Drive (R.E.M. song)">Drive</a>" by <a href="/wiki/R.E.M." title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a></li>
<li>"You're Never Over" contains a sample of "<a href="/wiki/Cry_Little_Sister" title="Cry Little Sister">Cry Little Sister</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Gerard_McMann" title="Gerard McMann" class="mw-redirect">Gerard McMann</a></li>
<li>"Untitled" features a sample of "<a href="/wiki/You_Don%27t_Own_Me" title="You Don't Own Me">You Don't Own Me</a>" as performed by <a href="/wiki/Lesley_Gore" title="Lesley Gore">Lesley Gore</a></li>
</ul>
